<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beyond_Low_Earth_Orbit_program_.282010.E2.80.93present.29">Beyond Low Earth Orbit program (2010–present)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg/170px-Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg/255px-Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg/340px-Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2880" data-file-height="3840" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Artist's rendering of the 70 mt variant of SLS launching Orion</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For missions beyond <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> (BLEO), NASA has been directed to develop the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> (SLS), a Saturn-V class rocket, and the two to six person, beyond low Earth orbit spacecraft, <a href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Orion spacecraft">Orion</a>. In February 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s administration proposed eliminating public funds for the <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation program</a> and shifting greater responsibility of servicing the ISS to private companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Achenbach_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Achenbach-94">[93]</a></sup> During a speech at the Kennedy Space Center on April 15, 2010, Obama proposed a new heavy-lift vehicle (HLV) to replace the formerly planned <a href="/wiki/Ares_V" title="Ares V">Ares V</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-speech_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-speech-95">[94]</a></sup> In his speech, Obama called for a manned mission to an asteroid as soon as 2025, and a manned mission to Mars orbit by the mid-2030s.<sup id="cite_ref-speech_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-speech-95">[94]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/NASA_Authorization_Act_of_2010" title="NASA Authorization Act of 2010">NASA Authorization Act of 2010</a> was passed by Congress and signed into law on October 11, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-nasa2010_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasa2010-96">[95]</a></sup> The act officially canceled the Constellation program.<sup id="cite_ref-nasa2010_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasa2010-96">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Authorization Act required a newly designed HLV be chosen within 90 days of its passing; the launch vehicle was given the name "Space Launch System". The new law also required the construction of a beyond low earth orbit spacecraft.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Orion spacecraft">Orion spacecraft</a>, which was being developed as part of the Constellation program, was chosen to fulfill this role.<sup id="cite_ref-authorizationact_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-authorizationact-98">[97]</a></sup> The Space Launch System is planned to launch both Orion and other necessary hardware for missions beyond low Earth orbit.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The SLS is to be upgraded over time with more powerful versions. The initial capability of SLS is required to be able to lift 70 mt into <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">LEO</a>. It is then planned to be upgraded to 105 mt and then eventually to 130 mt.<sup id="cite_ref-authorizationact_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-authorizationact-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schedule_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-100">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Exploration_Flight_Test_1" title="Exploration Flight Test 1">Exploration Flight Test 1</a> (EFT-1), an unmanned test flight of Orion's crew module, was launched on December 5, 2014, atop a <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV_Heavy" title="Delta IV Heavy">Delta IV Heavy</a> rocket.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-100">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_1" title="Exploration Mission 1">Exploration Mission-1</a> (EM-1) is the unmanned initial launch of SLS that would also send Orion on a <a href="/wiki/Circumlunar_trajectory" title="Circumlunar trajectory">circumlunar trajectory</a>, which is planned for 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-100">[99]</a></sup> The first manned flight of Orion and SLS, Exploration Mission 2 (EM-2) is to launch between 2019 and 2021; it is a 10- to 14-day mission planned to place a crew of four into <a href="/wiki/Lunar_orbit" title="Lunar orbit">Lunar orbit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-100">[99]</a></sup> As of March 2012, the destination for EM-3 and the intermediate focus for this new program is still in-flux.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 5, 2016, NASA and DARPA announced plans to build a series of new X-planes over the next 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Building_X_Planes_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Building_X_Planes-102">[101]</a></sup> One of the planes will reportedly be a supersonic vehicle that burns low-carbon <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a> and generates quiet sonic booms.<sup id="cite_ref-Building_X_Planes_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Building_X_Planes-102">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>NASA plans to build full scale deep space habitats as part of its <a href="/wiki/Next_Space_Technologies_for_Exploration_Partnerships" title="Next Space Technologies for Exploration Partnerships">Next Space Technologies for Exploration Partnerships</a> (NextSTEP) program.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unmanned_programs">Unmanned programs</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pioneer-3-4.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pioneer-3-4.gif/170px-Pioneer-3-4.gif" width="170" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pioneer-3-4.gif/255px-Pioneer-3-4.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/Pioneer-3-4.gif 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pioneer-3-4.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pioneer 3 and 4 launched in 1958 and 1959, respectively</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg/220px-JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg/330px-JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg/440px-JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1041" data-file-height="1560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
JWST main mirror assembled, November 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_NASA_missions" title="Unmanned NASA missions">Unmanned NASA missions</a></div>
<p>More than 1,000 unmanned missions have been designed to explore the Earth and the solar system.<sup id="cite_ref-NASAHisStat_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASAHisStat-104">[103]</a></sup> Besides exploration, communication satellites have also been launched by NASA.<sup id="cite_ref-NASAHis6_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASAHis6-105">[104]</a></sup> The missions have been launched directly from Earth or from orbiting space shuttles, which could either deploy the satellite itself, or with a rocket stage to take it farther.</p>
<p>The first US unmanned satellite was <a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a>, which started as an ABMA/JPL project during the early part of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>. It was launched in January 1958, two months after Sputnik. At the creation of NASA the Explorer project was transferred to this agency and still continues to this day. Its missions have been focusing on the Earth and the Sun, measuring magnetic fields and the <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">solar wind</a>, among other aspects.<sup id="cite_ref-NASAExp_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASAExp-106">[105]</a></sup> A more recent Earth mission, not related to the Explorer program, was the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a>, which as mentioned above was brought into orbit in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Inner_Solar_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Inner Solar System">inner Solar System</a> has been made the goal of at least four unmanned programs. The first was <a href="/wiki/Mariner_program" title="Mariner program">Mariner</a> in the 1960s and '70s, which made multiple visits to <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> and one to <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>. Probes launched under the Mariner program were also the first to make a planetary flyby (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_2" title="Mariner 2">Mariner 2</a>), to take the first pictures from another planet (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_4" title="Mariner 4">Mariner 4</a>), the first planetary orbiter (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_9" title="Mariner 9">Mariner 9</a>), and the first to make a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> maneuver (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_10" title="Mariner 10">Mariner 10</a>). This is a technique where the satellite takes advantage of the gravity and velocity of planets to reach its destination.<sup id="cite_ref-JPL_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPL-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first successful landing on Mars was made by <a href="/wiki/Viking_1" title="Viking 1">Viking 1</a> in 1976. Twenty years later a rover was landed on Mars by <a href="/wiki/Mars_Pathfinder" title="Mars Pathfinder">Mars Pathfinder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PlanetSocMars_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlanetSocMars-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Outside Mars, Jupiter was first visited by <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">Pioneer 10</a> in 1973. More than 20 years later <i><a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">Galileo</a></i> sent a probe into the planet's atmosphere, and became the first spacecraft to orbit the planet.<sup id="cite_ref-PlanetSocJup_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlanetSocJup-110">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">Pioneer 11</a> became the first spacecraft to visit <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> in 1979, with <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a> making the first (and so far only) visits to <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> in 1986 and 1989, respectively. The first spacecraft to leave the solar system was Pioneer 10 in 1983. For a time it was the most distant spacecraft, but it has since been surpassed by both <a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JPLVoyager_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPLVoyager-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pioneers 10 and 11 and both Voyager probes carry messages from the Earth to extraterrestrial life.<sup id="cite_ref-NASAPioneer10_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASAPioneer10-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JPLGolden_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPLGolden-113">[112]</a></sup> Communication can be difficult with deep space travel. For instance, it took about 3 hours for a radio signal to reach the New Horizons spacecraft when it was more than halfway to Pluto.<sup id="cite_ref-HeavensAbove_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeavensAbove-114">[113]</a></sup> Contact with Pioneer 10 was lost in 2003. Both Voyager probes continue to operate as they explore the outer boundary between the Solar System and interstellar space.<sup id="cite_ref-NASAVoyagesBeyond_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASAVoyagesBeyond-115">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 26, 2011, NASA's <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory</a> mission was successfully launched for Mars. <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity</a></i> successfully landed on Mars on August 6, 2012, and subsequently began its search for evidence of past or present life on Mars.<sup id="cite_ref-NASA-MSL_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-MSL-116">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-MSL_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-MSL-117">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_and_planned_activities">Recent and planned activities</span></h3>
<p>NASA's ongoing investigations include in-depth surveys of Mars (<a href="/wiki/Mars_2020" title="Mars 2020">Mars 2020</a> and <a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">InSight</a>) and Saturn and studies of the Earth and the Sun. Other active spacecraft missions are <a href="/wiki/Juno_(spacecraft)" title="Juno (spacecraft)">Juno</a> for <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini–Huygens">Cassini</a> for <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>, New Horizons (for Jupiter, <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a>, and beyond), and <a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">Dawn</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>. NASA continued to support <i><a href="/wiki/In_situ" title="In situ">in situ</a></i> exploration beyond the asteroid belt, including Pioneer and Voyager traverses into the unexplored trans-Pluto region, and <a href="/wiki/Gas_Giant" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas Giant">Gas Giant</a> orbiters Galileo (1989–2003), Cassini (1997–), and Juno (2011–).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a> mission to Pluto was launched in 2006 and successfully performed a flyby of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> on July 14, 2015. The probe received a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> in February 2007, examining some of Jupiter's inner moons and testing on-board instruments during the flyby. On the horizon of NASA's plans is the <a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a> spacecraft as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Scout_Program" title="Mars Scout Program">Mars Scout Program</a> to study the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">atmosphere of Mars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MAVEN_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAVEN-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg/220px-Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg/330px-Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg/440px-Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1090" data-file-height="1350" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vision mission for an interstellar precursor spacecraft by NASA</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On December 4, 2006, NASA announced it was planning a <a href="/wiki/Lunar_outpost_(NASA)" title="Lunar outpost (NASA)">permanent moon base</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-moon2_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moon2-120">[119]</a></sup> The goal was to start building the moon base by 2020, and by 2024, have a fully functional base that would allow for crew rotations and <a href="/wiki/In-situ_resource_utilization" class="mw-redirect" title="In-situ resource utilization">in-situ resource utilization</a>. However, in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Review_of_United_States_Human_Space_Flight_Plans_Committee" title="Review of United States Human Space Flight Plans Committee">Augustine Committee</a> found the program to be on a "unsustainable trajectory."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> In 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> halted existing plans, including the Moon base, and directed a generic focus on manned missions to asteroids and Mars, as well as extending support for the International Space Station.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2011, NASA's strategic goals have been<sup id="cite_ref-NP-2011-01-699-HQ_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NP-2011-01-699-HQ-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Extend and sustain <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human activities</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Solar_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar system">solar system</a></li>
<li>Expand scientific understanding of the Earth and the universe</li>
<li>Create innovative new space <a href="/wiki/Technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Technologies">technologies</a></li>
<li>Advance <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a> research</li>
<li>Enable program and institutional capabilities to conduct NASA's aeronautics and space activities</li>
<li>Share NASA with the public, educators, and students to provide opportunities to participate</li>
</ul>
<p>In August 2011, NASA accepted the donation of <a href="/wiki/2012_National_Reconnaissance_Office_space_telescope_donation_to_NASA" title="2012 National Reconnaissance Office space telescope donation to NASA">two space telescopes</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Reconnaissance_Office" title="National Reconnaissance Office">National Reconnaissance Office</a>. Despite being stored unused, the instruments are superior to the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-popsci-2012_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popsci-2012-124">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2011, NASA announced the start of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> program to develop a human-rated heavy lift vehicle. The Space Launch System is intended to launch the <a href="/wiki/Orion_Multi-Purpose_Crew_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle">Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle</a> and other elements towards the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Near-Earth_asteroids" class="mw-redirect" title="Near-Earth asteroids">near-Earth asteroids</a>, and one day <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> The Orion MPCV conducted an unmanned test launch on a <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV_Heavy" title="Delta IV Heavy">Delta IV Heavy</a> rocket in December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope" title="James Webb Space Telescope">James Webb Space Telescope</a> is currently scheduled to launch in late 2018.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/220px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/330px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/440px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)"><i>Curiosity's</i></a> wheel on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On August 6, 2012, NASA landed the rover <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity</a></i> on Mars. On August 27, 2012, <i>Curiosity</i> transmitted the first pre-recorded message from the surface of Mars back to Earth, made by Administrator Charlie Bolden:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Hello. This is Charlie Bolden, NASA Administrator, speaking to you via the broadcast capabilities of the Curiosity Rover, which is now on the surface of Mars.
<p>Since the beginning of time, humankind’s curiosity has led us to constantly seek new life...new possibilities just beyond the horizon. I want to congratulate the men and women of our NASA family as well as our commercial and government partners around the world, for taking us a step beyond to Mars.<br />
This is an extraordinary achievement. Landing a rover on Mars is not easy&#160;– others have tried&#160;– only America has fully succeeded. The investment we are making...the knowledge we hope to gain from our observation and analysis of Gale Crater, will tell us much about the possibility of life on Mars as well as the past and future possibilities for our own planet. Curiosity will bring benefits to Earth and inspire a new generation of scientists and explorers, as it prepares the way for a human mission in the not too distant future. Thank you.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_research">Scientific research</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/220px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/330px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/440px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Radioisotope within a graphite shell that goes into the generator.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NASA_research" title="NASA research">NASA research</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For technologies funded or otherwise supported by NASA, see <a href="/wiki/NASA_spin-off_technologies" title="NASA spin-off technologies">NASA spin-off technologies</a>.</div>
<p>NASA's <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics_Research_Mission_Directorate" title="Aeronautics Research Mission Directorate">Aeronautics Research Mission Directorate</a> conducts aeronautics research.</p>
<p>NASA has made use of technologies such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Multi-Mission_Radioisotope_Thermoelectric_Generator" title="Multi-Mission Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator">Multi-Mission Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator</a></i> (MMRTG), which is a type of <a href="/wiki/Radioisotope_thermoelectric_generator" title="Radioisotope thermoelectric generator">Radioisotope thermoelectric generator</a> used on space missions.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> Shortages of this material have curtailed deep space missions since the turn of the millennia.<sup id="cite_ref-lpi.usra.edu_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpi.usra.edu-129">[128]</a></sup> An example of a spacecraft that was not developed because of a shortage of this material was <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons_2" title="New Horizons 2">New Horizons 2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lpi.usra.edu_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpi.usra.edu-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earth science research program was created and first funded in the 1980s under the administrations of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" class="mw-redirect" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_study">Climate study</span></h3>
<p>NASA also researches and publishes on <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> issues.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> Its statements concur with the interpretation that the global climate is heating.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Smith_Walker" title="Robert Smith Walker">Bob Walker</a>, who has advised president-elect <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> on space issues, has advocated that NASA should focus on space exploration and that its climate study operations should be transferred to other agencies such as <a href="/wiki/NOAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff_and_leadership">Staff and leadership</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_NASA_Administrators" class="mw-redirect" title="List of NASA Administrators">List of NASA Administrators</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg/170px-Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg/255px-Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg/340px-Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2513" data-file-height="3190" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bolden_speaks_at_STS-135_wheels_stop_event.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charles Bolden speaks after landing of the last Space Shuttle mission, <a href="/wiki/STS-135" title="STS-135">STS-135</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The agency's leader, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Administrators_and_Deputy_Administrators_of_NASA" title="List of Administrators and Deputy Administrators of NASA">NASA's administrator</a>, is nominated by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> subject to approval of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">US Senate</a>, and reports to him or her and serves as senior space science advisor. Though space exploration is ostensibly non-partisan, the appointee usually is associated with the President's political party (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>), and a new administrator is usually chosen when the Presidency changes parties. Though the agency is independent, the survival or discontinuation of projects can depend directly on the will of the President.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-135">[134]</a></sup> The agency's administration is located at <a href="/wiki/NASA_Headquarters" title="NASA Headquarters">NASA Headquarters</a> in Washington, DC and provides overall guidance and direction.<sup id="cite_ref-HQ_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQ-136">[135]</a></sup> Except under exceptional circumstances, NASA civil service employees are required to be <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizenship in the United States">citizens of the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first administrator was Dr. <a href="/wiki/T._Keith_Glennan" title="T. Keith Glennan">T. Keith Glennan</a> appointed by Republican President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>. During his term he brought together the disparate projects in American space development research.<sup id="cite_ref-glennan_biography_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glennan_biography-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>The third administrator, <a href="/wiki/James_E._Webb" title="James E. Webb">James E. Webb</a> (1961–1968), appointed by President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, was a Democrat who first publicly served under President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>. In order to implement the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a> to achieve Kennedy's Moon landing goal by the end of the 1960s, Webb directed major management restructuring and facility expansion, establishing the Houston Manned Spacecraft (Johnson) Center and the Florida Launch Operations (Kennedy) Center. Capitalizing on Kennedy's legacy, President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> kept continuity with the Apollo program by keeping Webb on when he succeeded Kennedy in November 1963. But Webb resigned in October 1968 before Apollo achieved its goal, and Republican President <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Nixon" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard M. Nixon">Richard M. Nixon</a> replaced Webb with Republican <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Paine" title="Thomas O. Paine">Thomas O. Paine</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/James_C._Fletcher" title="James C. Fletcher">James C. Fletcher</a>, appointed in 1971 by President Nixon, was responsible for early planning of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle program</a> during his first term as administrator through May 1977. He was appointed for a second term as administrator from May 1986 through April 1989 by President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> to help the agency recover from the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">Space Shuttle <i>Challenger</i> accident</a>.</p>
<p>Former <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronaut</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bolden" title="Charles Bolden">Charles Bolden</a> served as NASA's twelfth administrator from July 2009 to January 20, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-confirmed_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-confirmed-139">[138]</a></sup> Administrator Bolden is one of three former astronauts who became NASA administrators, along with <a href="/wiki/Richard_H._Truly" title="Richard H. Truly">Richard H. Truly</a> (served 1989–1992) and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_D._Gregory" title="Frederick D. Gregory">Frederick D. Gregory</a> (acting, 2005).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:348px;max-width:348px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Jet Propulsion Laboratory complex in Pasadena, California" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/170px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg" width="170" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/255px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/340px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2867" data-file-height="2242" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> complex in Pasadena, California</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Vehicle Assembly Building and Launch Control Center at Kennedy Space Center" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/170px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg" width="170" height="131" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/255px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/340px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1499" data-file-height="1151" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Vehicle Assembly and Launch Control at <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NASA_facilities" title="NASA facilities">NASA facilities</a></div>
<p>NASA's facilities are research, construction and communication centers to help its missions. Some facilities serve more than one application for historic or administrative reasons. NASA also operates a short-line <a href="/wiki/NASA_Railroad" title="NASA Railroad">railroad at the Kennedy Space Center</a> and own special aircraft, for instance two <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Carrier_Aircraft" title="Shuttle Carrier Aircraft">Boeing 747 that transport Space Shuttle orbiter</a>.</p>
<p>John F. Kennedy Space Center (KSC), is one of the best-known NASA facilities. It has been the launch site for every United States human space flight since 1968. Although such flights are currently on pause, KSC continues to manage and operate unmanned rocket launch facilities for America's civilian space program from three pads at the adjoining Cape Canaveral Air Force Station.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a> (JSC) in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center</a>, where all flight control is managed for manned space missions. JSC is the lead NASA center for activities regarding the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> and also houses the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Corps" title="NASA Astronaut Corps">NASA Astronaut Corps</a> that selects, trains, and provides astronauts as crew members for US and international space missions.</p>
<p>Another major facility is <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">Marshall Space Flight Center</a> in Huntsville, Alabama at which the Saturn 5 rocket and Skylab were developed.<sup id="cite_ref-NASAMSFC_Fact_sheet_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASAMSFC_Fact_sheet-140">[139]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">JPL</a> worked together with <a href="/wiki/Army_Ballistic_Missile_Agency" title="Army Ballistic Missile Agency">ABMA</a>, one of the agencies behind <a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a>, the first American space mission.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/220px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/330px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/440px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center#FCR_1_.282006-present.29" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">FCR 1</a> in 2009 during the <a href="/wiki/STS-128" title="STS-128">STS-128</a> mission, JSC in Houston</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ten NASA field centers are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">John F. Kennedy Space Center</a>, Florida</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">Ames Research Center</a>, Moffett Field, California</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Flight_Research_Center" title="Armstrong Flight Research Center">Armstrong Flight Research Center</a> (formerly Hugh L. Dryden Flight Research Facility), Edwards, California</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, Greenbelt, Maryland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a>, near Pasadena, California</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a>, Houston, Texas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Langley_Research_Center" title="Langley Research Center">Langley Research Center</a>, Hampton, Virginia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_H._Glenn_Research_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="John H. Glenn Research Center">John H. Glenn Research Center</a>, Cleveland, Ohio</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="George C. Marshall Space Flight Center">George C. Marshall Space Flight Center</a>, Huntsville, Alabama</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_C._Stennis_Space_Center" title="John C. Stennis Space Center">John C. Stennis Space Center</a>, Bay St. Louis, Mississippi</li>
</ul>
<p>Numerous other facilities are operated by NASA, including the <a href="/wiki/Wallops_Flight_Facility" title="Wallops Flight Facility">Wallops Flight Facility</a> in Wallops Island, Virginia; the <a href="/wiki/Michoud_Assembly_Facility" title="Michoud Assembly Facility">Michoud Assembly Facility</a> in New Orleans, Louisiana; the <a href="/wiki/White_Sands_Test_Facility" title="White Sands Test Facility">White Sands Test Facility</a> in Las Cruces, New Mexico; and <a href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Deep Space Network">Deep Space Network</a> stations in <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Goldstone Deep Space Communications Complex">Barstow</a>, California; <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Madrid Deep Space Communications Complex">Madrid</a>, Spain; and <a href="/wiki/Canberra_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" class="mw-redirect" title="Canberra Deep Space Communications Complex">Canberra</a>, Australia.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NASA-Budget-Federal.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/220px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/330px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/440px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="585" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NASA-Budget-Federal.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
NASA's budget from 1958 to 2012 as a percentage of federal budget</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jsc2004e18852.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/220px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/330px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/440px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3555" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jsc2004e18852.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An artist's conception, from NASA, of an astronaut planting a US flag on Mars. A <a href="/wiki/Manned_mission_to_Mars" class="mw-redirect" title="Manned mission to Mars">manned mission to Mars</a> has been discussed as a possible NASA mission since the 1960s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_NASA" title="Budget of NASA">Budget of NASA</a></div>
<p>NASA's budget has generally been approximately 1% of the federal budget from the early 1970s on, after briefly peaking at approximately 4.41% in 1966 during the Apollo program.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Public perception of NASA's budget has differed significantly from reality; a 1997 poll indicated that most Americans responded that 20% of the federal budget went to NASA.<sup id="cite_ref-perception_of_US_Human_Spaceflight_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perception_of_US_Human_Spaceflight-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>The percentage of federal budget that NASA has been allocated has been steadily dropping since the Apollo program and in 2012 it was estimated at 0.48% of the federal budget.<sup id="cite_ref-B2013_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B2013-143">[142]</a></sup> In a March 2012 meeting of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Commerce,_Science_and_Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senate Committee on Commerce, Science and Transportation">United States Senate Science Committee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson" title="Neil deGrasse Tyson">Neil deGrasse Tyson</a> testified that "Right now, NASA’s annual budget is half a penny on your tax dollar. For twice that—a penny on a dollar—we can transform the country from a sullen, dispirited nation, weary of economic struggle, to one where it has reclaimed its 20th century birthright to dream of tomorrow."<sup id="cite_ref-tysontranscript_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tysontranscript-144">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tysontranscript_video_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tysontranscript_video-145">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>For Fiscal Year 2015, NASA received an appropriation of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$18.01 billion</span> from Congress—$549 million more than requested and approximately $350 million more than the 2014 NASA budget passed by Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-sfn20141214_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfn20141214-146">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span></h2>
<p>The exhaust gases produced by rocket propulsion systems, both in Earth's atmosphere and in space, can adversely effect the Earth's environment. Some <a href="/wiki/Hypergolic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypergolic">hypergolic</a> rocket propellants, such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrazine" title="Hydrazine">hydrazine</a>, are highly toxic prior to <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">combustion</a>, but decompose into less toxic compounds after burning. Rockets using hydrocarbon fuels, such as <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a>, release carbon dioxide and soot in their exhaust.<sup id="cite_ref-rocket_soot_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocket_soot-147">[146]</a></sup> However, carbon dioxide emissions are insignificant compared to those from other sources; on average, the United States consumed 802,620,000 US gallons (3.0382<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;L) gallons of liquid fuels per day in 2014, while a single <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">Falcon 9</a> rocket first stage burns around 25,000 US gallons (95,000&#160;L) of <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> fuel per launch.<sup id="cite_ref-EIA_2016_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA_2016-148">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Even if a Falcon 9 were launched every single day, it would only represent 0.006% of liquid fuel consumption (and carbon dioxide emissions) for that day. Additionally, the exhaust from <a href="/wiki/LOx" class="mw-redirect" title="LOx">LOx</a>- and <a href="/wiki/LH2" class="mw-redirect" title="LH2">LH2</a>- fueled engines, like the <a href="/wiki/SSME" class="mw-redirect" title="SSME">SSME</a>, is almost entirely water vapor.<sup id="cite_ref-NASA-SSME_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-SSME-150">[149]</a></sup> NASA addressed environmental concerns with its canceled <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation program</a> in accordance with the National Environmental Policy Act in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-NASA-Constellation_Program_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-Constellation_Program-151">[150]</a></sup> In contrast, <a href="/wiki/Ion_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Ion engines">ion engines</a> use harmless noble gases like <a href="/wiki/Xenon" title="Xenon">xenon</a> for propulsion.<sup id="cite_ref-ns20070928_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ns20070928-152">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Goto2003_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goto2003-153">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 8, 2003, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> recognized NASA as the first federal agency to directly use <a href="/wiki/Landfill_gas" title="Landfill gas">landfill gas</a> to produce energy at one of its facilities—the <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, Greenbelt, Maryland.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>An example of NASA's environmental efforts is the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Sustainability_Base" title="NASA Sustainability Base">NASA Sustainability Base</a>. Additionally, the Exploration Sciences Building was awarded the LEED Gold rating in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup></p>

Left, top-down: Spacecraft of Apollo, Gemini and Mercury. The <a href="/wiki/Saturn_IB" title="Saturn IB">Saturn IB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mercury-Redstone_Launch_Vehicle" title="Mercury-Redstone Launch Vehicle">Mercury-Redstone</a> launch vehicles are left out.</span></li>
